Hailed by Time as &amp;quot;brilliant literary comedy as well as a brilliant sketch of the times,&amp;quot; A Dance to the Music of Time opens just after World War I. Amid the fever of the 1920s and the first chill of the 1930s, Nick Jenkins and his friends confront sex, society, business, and art. In the second volume they move to London in a whirl of marriage and adulteries, fashions and frivolities, personal triumphs and failures. These books &amp;quot;provide an unsurpassed picture, at once gay and melancholy, of social and artistic life in Britain between the wars&amp;quot; (Arthur Schlesinger, Jr.). The third volume follows Nick into army life and evokes London during the blitz. In the climactic final volume, England has won the war and must now count the losses.\n\nFour very different young men on the threshold of manhood dominate this opening volume of A Dance to the Music of Time. The narrator, Jenkins—a budding writer—shares a room with Templer, already a passionate womanizer, and Stringham, aristocratic and reckless. Widermerpool, as hopelessly awkward as he is intensely ambitious, lurks on the periphery of their world. Amid the fever of the 1920s and the first chill of the 1930s, these four gain their initiations into sex, society, business, and art. Considered a masterpiece of modern fiction, Powell\'s epic creates a rich panorama of life in England between the wars.\n\nIncludes these novels: \nA Question of Upbringing \nA Buyer\'s Market \nThe The time of the novel is the closing months of the most senselessly savage of modern conflicts. In France, millions of men engaged in brutal trench warfare are all &amp;quot;ghosts in the making.&amp;quot; In England, psychologist William Rivers, with severe pangs of conscience, treats the mental casualties of the war to make them whole enough to fight again. One of these, Billy Prior, risen to the officer class from the working class, both courageous and sardonic, decides to return to France with his fellow officer, poet Wilfred Owen, to fight a war he no longer believes in. Meanwhile, Rivers, enfevered by influenza, returns in memory to his experience studying a South Pacific tribe whose ethos amounted to a culture of death. Across the gulf between his society and theirs, Rivers begins to form connections that cast new light on his--and our--understanding of war. Combining poetic intensity with gritty realism, blending biting humor with tragic drama, moving toward a denouement as inevitable as it is devastating, The Ghost Road both encapsulates history and transcends it.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1169504.A_S_Byatt">About A.S. Byatt</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1169504.A_S_Byatt"><img alt="1169504" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1388376297p2/1169504.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6742045159599156233">A.S. Byatt (Antonia Susan Byatt) is internationally known for her novels and short stories. Her novels include the <strong>Booker Prize</strong> winner <em>Possession</em>, <em>The Biographer’s Tale and the quartet</em>, <em>The Virgin in the Garden</em>, <em>Still Life</em>, <em>Babel Tower</em> and <em>A Whistling Woman</em>, and her highly acclaimed collections of short stories include <em>Sugar and Other Stories</em>, <em>The Matisse Stories</em>, <em>The Djinn in the Nightingale’s Ey</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6742045159599156233">A.S. Byatt (Antonia Susan Byatt) is internationally known for her novels and short stories. Her novels include the <strong>Booker Prize</strong> winner <em>Possession</em>, <em>The Biographer’s Tale and the quartet</em>, <em>The Virgin in the Garden</em>, <em>Still Life</em>, <em>Babel Tower</em> and <em>A Whistling Woman</em>, and her highly acclaimed collections of short stories include <em>Sugar and Other Stories</em>, <em>The Matisse Stories</em>, <em>The Djinn in the Nightingale’s Eye</em>, <em>Elementals</em> and her most recent book <em>Little Black Book of Stories</em>. A distinguished critic as well as a writer of fiction, A S Byatt was appointed CBE in 1990 and DBE in 1999.<br /><br />BYATT, Dame Antonia (Susan), (Dame Antonia Duffy), DBE 1999 (CBE 1990); FRSL 1983; Chevalier de l’Ordre des Arts et des Lettres (France), 2003 , writer; born 24 Aug. 1936;<br /><br />Daughter of His Honour John Frederick Drabble, QC and late Kathleen Marie Bloor<br /><br />Byatt has famously been engaged in a long-running feud with her novelist sister, <a title="Margaret Drabble" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/60750.Margaret_Drabble">Margaret Drabble</a>, over the alleged appropriation of a family tea-set in one of her novels. The pair seldom see each other and each does not read the books of the other.<br /><br />Married<br />1st, 1959, Ian Charles Rayner Byatt (Sir I. C. R. Byatt) marriage dissolved. 1969; one daughter (one son deceased)<br />2nd, 1969, Peter John Duffy; two daughters.<br /><br />Education<br />Sheffield High School; The Mount School, York; Newnham College, Cambridge (BA Hons; Hon. Fellow 1999); Bryn Mawr College, Philadelphia, USA; Somerville College, Oxford.<br /><br />Academic Honours:<br />Hon. Fellow, London Inst., 2000; Fellow UCL, 2004<br />Hon. DLitt: Bradford, 1987; DUniv York, 1991; Durham, 1991; Nottingham, 1992; Liverpool, 1993; Portsmouth, 1994; London, 1995; Sheffield, 2000; Kent 2004; Hon. LittD Cambridge, 1999<br /><br />Prizes<br />The PEN/Macmillan Silver Pen Of Fiction prize, 1986 for STILL LIFE<br />The Booker Prize, 1990, for POSSESSION<br />Irish Times/Aer Lingus International Fiction Prize, 1990 for POSSESSION<br />The Eurasian section of Best Book in Commonwealth Prize, 1991 for POSSESSION<br />Premio Malaparte, Capri, 1995;<br />Mythopoeic Fantasy Award for Adult Literature, California, 1998 for THE DJINN IN THE NIGHTINGALE''S EYE<br />Shakespeare Prize, Toepfer Foundation, Hamburg, 2002;<br /><br />Publications:<br />The Shadow of the Sun, 1964;<br />Degrees of Freedom, 1965 (reprinted as Degrees of Freedom: the early novels of Iris Murdoch, 1994);<br />The Game, 1967;<br />Wordsworth and Coleridge in their Time, 1970 (reprinted as Unruly Times: Wordsworth and Coleridge in their Time, 1989);<br />Iris Murdoch 1976<br />The Virgin in the Garden, 1978;<br />GEORGE ELIOT Selected Essays, Poems and Other Writings , 1979 (editor);<br />Still Life, 1985<br />Sugar and Other Stories, 1987;<br />George Eliot: selected essays, 1989 (editor)<br />Possession: a romance, 1990<br />Robert Browning''s Dramatic Monologues, 1990 (editor);<br />Passions of the Mind, (essays), 1991;<br />Angels and Insects (novellae),1992<br />The Matisse Stories (short stories),1993;<br />The Djinn in the Nightingale''s Eye: five fairy stories, 1994<br />Imagining Characters, 1995 (joint editor);<br />New Writing 4, 1995 (joint editor);<br />Babel Tower, 1996;<br />New Writing 6, 1997 (joint editor);<br />The Oxford Book of English Short Stories, 1998 (editor);<br />Elementals: Stories of fire and ice (short stories), 1998;<br />The Biographer''s Tale, 2000;<br />On Histories and Stories (essays), 2000;<br />Portraits in Fiction, 2001;<br />The Bird Hand Book, 2001 (Photographs by Victor Schrager Text By AS Byatt);<br />A Whistling Woman, 2002<br />Little </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6742045159599156233">...more</a>
